You MUST use the Sourcegraph MCP tools (keyword_search, finder, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read) to explore and understand this codebase. You are REQUIRED to use these tools extensively — they are your primary means of code discovery.

Sourcegraph repository: `github.com/django/django` (use `repo:^github.com/django/django$` filter in keyword_search)

**REQUIRED WORKFLOW:**
1. FIRST use Sourcegraph tools (keyword_search, finder, list_files) to explore the codebase structure and find relevant code
2. Use go_to_definition and find_references to trace code relationships
3. After finding code via Sourcegraph, use Read to verify actual local contents before editing
4. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
5. Use `deepsearch` for complex architectural questions — it returns a polling link, NOT immediate results
6. After calling `deepsearch`, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times (Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete)

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide with detailed usage for each tool.

# Investigation: Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit

**Repository:** django/django
**Task Type:** Migration Audit (investigation only — no code changes)

## Scenario

Django is changing the `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from their current format of `[(name, email), ...]` tuples to simple `[email, ...]` string lists. This is tracked in ticket #36138. Before executing this migration, the team needs a comprehensive audit of all code that reads, validates, or processes these settings.

## Your Task

Produce a migration audit report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Every file that reads `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`
2. Every file that validates or type-checks the settings format
3. Every file that unpacks the tuple format (e.g., `for name, email in settings.ADMINS`)
4. All documentation references that show the old tuple format
5. Test files that use the old format in fixtures or assertions
6. Third-party compatibility concerns (what breaks for users with old-format settings)
7. A migration checklist: each file that needs changes, what change is needed

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Core code paths that consume the tuple format>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of modules/packages impacted>

## Recommendation
<Migration checklist with specific files and changes needed>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `django/core/mail/`, test files, and documentation

84-assistanttext-
Perfect! I have completed a comprehensive audit investigation of the Django codebase regarding the ADMINS/MANAGERS settings format migration. Let me summarize what was found:

## Investigation Complete

I've created a detailed migration audit report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here are the key findings:

### **Summary**
The ADMINS and MANAGERS settings are transitioning from tuple format `(name, email)` to simple string format `[email, ...]`. The tuple format was deprecated in Django 6.0 with a deprecation warning and is scheduled for removal in Django 7.0.

### **Core Implementation Points**
1. **Single validation point**: `django/core/mail/__init__.py` in the `_send_server_message()` function handles all format detection and validation
2. **Backward compatibility**: Lines 165-173 detect old tuple format and warn; this code must be removed in Django 7.0
3. **Validation logic**: Lines 175-180 enforce that settings are lists/tuples of email strings

### **Components Using ADMINS/MANAGERS**
- Mail functions: `mail_admins()`, `mail_managers()`
- Logging: `AdminEmailHandler` 
- Middleware: `BrokenLinkEmailsMiddleware` (sends 404 notifications to MANAGERS)
- Management command: `sendtestemail`

### **Files Requiring Changes for Django 7.0 Migration**
1. **`django/core/mail/__init__.py`** - Remove deprecation warning block (lines 165-173)
2. **`tests/mail/tests.py`** - Remove `test_deprecated_admins_managers_tuples()` test
3. **`docs/internals/deprecation.txt`** - Remove future removal notice (lines 34-35)
4. **`docs/ref/settings.txt`** - Remove version note from MANAGERS section

The report includes a complete checklist, code examples, and migration guidance for third-party compatibility impacts.

32. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit Report\n\n## Summary\n\nDjango is transitioning `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from tuple format `[(name, email), ...]` to string-list format `[email, ...]`. The tuple format was deprecated in Django 6.0 and is scheduled for removal in Django 7.0. `django/core/management/commands/sendtestemail.py` | No changes - delegates to mail functions |\n| Documentation | `docs/internals/deprecation.txt` | Remove lines 34-35 |\n| Documentation | # Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit Report

## Summary

Django is transitioning `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from tuple format `[(name, email), ...]` to string-list format `[email, ...]`. The tuple format was deprecated in Django 6.0 and is scheduled for removal in Django 7.0. All code that reads, validates, or processes these settings requires analysis for impact.

## Root Cause & Core Implementation

The primary consumption point is in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` at the `_send_server_message()` function (lines 152-192), which is called by both `mail_admins()` and `mail_managers()` functions. This function contains:

1. **Lines 165-173**: Backward-compatibility handling that detects old tuple format and issues `RemovedInDjango70Warning` deprecation warning
2. **Lines 175-180**: Validation that ensures settings are lists/tuples of email address strings

The validation logic (lines 175-180) checks:
- Setting is a list or tuple
- Each element is a string or Promise object
- Raises `ImproperlyConfigured` if format is incorrect

## Evidence: Complete File Listing

All files that read, validate, or reference ADMINS/MANAGERS settings:

### Core Implementation (3 files)

| File | Lines | Purpose | Current Behavior |
|------|-------|---------|------------------|
| `django/core/mail/__init__.py` | 165-173 | Old tuple detection and warning | Warns if `(name, email)` tuples detected |
| `django/core/mail/__init__.py` | 175-180 | Format validation | Validates list of email strings |
| `django/core/mail/__init__.py` | 197-225 | `mail_admins()` and `mail_managers()` | Call `_send_server_message()` with setting name |

### Logging Handler (2 files)

| File | Lines | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| `django/utils/log.py` | 97 | `AdminEmailHandler.emit(
... (truncated)
